Step 18: You now need to repeat the Input, Process and Output for the second stage or process attached to the routing of this product. You will select the next tab which resembles the next step in the process.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/1084d037-f14b-4b05-83bb-89bd4f1176c1/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=290,187
You output from the previous process will act as the input for the current process.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/d76ebc3b-505e-48a2-b824-d33edfd54841/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=309,132
Step 19: You need to select the assembly or output at this stage.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/3860923d-9820-4fb8-9476-cece250c01bc/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=16,63&br_px=3456,1986&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=1014,390

Step 20: Since this is the final stage of the route, you need to select the output destination, which is the final assembly warehouse area type.

Once again, you can add a description of the final state.

The route has now been created and the product can be scheduled for production.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/cd0ae444-57e9-407d-9981-2b327e5f1105/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=310,143

	•	Create Sub Contracted Routes
Step 1: Select "Routing"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/d5b878d0-aa9c-4df0-9d25-767afd19764c/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=419,171
Step 2: Select "Sub Contracted Routes"

Sales Overview
Sales Module Description
This module manages all aspects of the sales process, including customer relationship management, sales orders, invoicing, pricing, and revenue tracking. It's essential for managing customer interactions and sales transactions effectively. It also allows for the effective management of both internal and external staff.
Sales Module Process Flow
￼
Sales Quote: A sales quote is a document provided to a potential customer that outlines the estimated cost of a product or service. It includes details such as the quantity, unit price, and total price of the items being quoted. Sales quotes are typically used to initiate the sales process and provide customers with an understanding of the pricing for their desired products or services.
Sales Order: A sales order is a formal request made by a customer to purchase goods or services. It includes specific details such as the quantity, description, and agreed-upon price of the items being ordered. Sales orders are generated based on the customer's acceptance of a sales quote and serve as a confirmation of the purchase.
Fulfilment Order: A fulfilment order is created to initiate the process of fulfilling a customer's order. It includes information about the items to be shipped, their quantities, and any special instructions related to packaging or delivery. Fulfilment orders are typically used by warehouse or fulfilment teams to pick, pack, and ship the ordered items to the customer.
Sales Invoice: A sales invoice is a document sent to the customer after the products or services have been delivered. It includes detailed information such as the itemized list of products or services provided, quantities, prices, any applicable taxes, and the total amount due. Sales invoices serve as a formal request for payment and provide a record of the transaction.
The process from a sales quote to a sales order to fulfilment and finally to a sales invoice involves the following steps: A sales quote is created and sent to the customer, outlining the estimated cost of the requested products or services. Once the customer accepts the quote, a sales order is generated, confirming the purchase.
The procurement team will create a production plan based on the sales order products, assemblies or items and their associated quantities. Upon production completion, the fulfilment team then prepares a fulfilment order, picking and packing the items for shipment. After the items are delivered to the customer, a sales invoice is generated and sent to request payment for the completed transaction.
Sales Sub Modules
	•	Sales Personnel
Sales personnel are internal employees who earn either a wage or a combination of wage and commission to sell manufactured products to current or prospective customers.
They have access to a personalized dashboard and are responsible for managing the sales cycle and customer relationships.
Sales employees can create quotes, sales orders, sales invoices and customer within their allocate permissions and dashboard.

	•	Customer Management
Customer management involves the creation and oversight of active, inactive, and prospective customer leads. Each customer has a dedicated profile and dashboard for assessing insightful metrics, and sales cycles can be initiated directly from their dashboard.

	•	Sales Order Management
Sales order management is a global module which handles and oversees customer orders from initial quotation to final invoicing. It involves creating quotes, converting them into sales orders, generating invoices, and tracking the progress of purchased assemblies, products, and items as they move through production. This ensures that all aspects of the sales order, from pricing and order details to production status and delivery schedules, are efficiently managed and monitored, providing a seamless experience for both the sales team and the customer.

	•	Customer Returns
The ArcFlow Customer Return feature enables you to manage the entire return process efficiently. It allows customers to request return authorizations and facilitates the receipt and inspection of returned items. The feature supports processing refunds or replacements and updating inventory records accordingly. It also provides detailed tracking and reporting on return reasons and statuses, ensuring that returns are handled swiftly and accurately to maintain customer satisfaction.

	•	Sales Configurations
The Sales Configuration module in our system allows you to set up and manage pricing structures, including price breaks and percentage discounts. These discounts can be assigned to sellable products, assemblies, and individual items, or directly to specific customers. This flexibility enables you to create tailored pricing strategies that cater to various customer segments and sales scenarios, ensuring competitive and attractive pricing for your products while maximizing profitability and customer satisfaction.

	•	Warranties
Our warranty system enables you to efficiently manage product warranties by tracking warranty terms and conditions for each item sold. It allows you to register warranty details at the time of sale, monitor warranty periods, and handle claims and repairs. The system also supports the processing of replacements or refunds under warranty and provides comprehensive reporting on warranty claims and statuses, ensuring that both customers and internal teams have clear visibility and management of warranty-related activities.

	•	Sales History
Our Sales History module provides a comprehensive record of all past sales transactions. It allows you to view detailed information on each sale, including product details, quantities, prices, customer information, and dates of transactions.

	•	Dashboard
The Sales Dashboard sub-module on the ArcFlow ERP system provides a real-time overview of sales performance through visual charting and metric collection. Users can filter date ranges to customize the displayed data. The dashboard tracks metrics such as sales volume, highest-performing sellable products, assemblies, and items, and shows customer segments based on sales volume. This comprehensive view helps businesses quickly assess their sales activities and make informed decisions.

Sales Personnel
Overview Description:
The ArcFlow Sales Personnel Sub-Module is designed for employees who earn either a wage or a combination of wage and commission. These sales personnel manage the relationship between the company and their customers, actively selling products and addressing customer needs. They can initiate quotes, sales orders, and invoices, as well as monitor the status of order fulfillment. Additionally, they have access to personalized dashboards that enable them to track their performance and gain insights into their sales trends, optimizing their sales activities and customer interactions.

	•	Create Sales Quote

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/014d7964-51a2-4033-8068-9145971825e5/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,393&br_px=859,874&force_format=png&width=860&wat_scale=76&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=241,212

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/7409bee2-40cb-4ce6-ba50-72541d980f55/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=275,392&br_px=1135,873&force_format=png&width=860&wat_scale=76&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=402,212

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/7bf1902e-ea08-44b4-9d44-c65449f320bf/user_cropped_screenshot.jpeg?tl_px=2,344&br_px=2296,1625&force_format=png&width=1120.0
11\. Click "Create" to create the invoice. This will also

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/f341f7b9-97d5-4f80-ad9f-18cc489a2dcd/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=5,0&br_px=2299,1281&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=1035,186

	•	Create Sales Order
1\. There are 2 ways to create a Sales Order. You can either convert a Sales Quote directly to a Sales Order or you can make a Sales Order from scratch. To convert a quote you go to the sales quote page and then click this button to convert the quote to a Sales Order.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/55f3d8af-01fa-45df-aaa4-2a71b263af53/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=5,0&br_px=2299,1281&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=893,188

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/9d7c7b87-8fe9-4af6-b8c2-f010597bcd09/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=5,0&br_px=2299,1281&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=1041,38

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/8c2b2e10-259d-4590-87ba-2ba43b24208a/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,143&br_px=859,624&force_format=png&width=860&wat_scale=76&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=325,212
4\. Click "Create Sales Order"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/2d19deda-1d1c-47e9-af7e-7793f4c9f4ed/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1439,24&br_px=2299,505&force_format=png&width=860&wat_scale=76&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=651,212

	•	Create Sales Invoice
1\. Click "Create Invoice"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/f7455c6a-9844-434d-9961-0c6f13e8ba77/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=5,0&br_px=2299,1281&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=1004,109

Customer Management
Overview Description:
The ArcFlow Customer Management Sub-Module, customer management encompasses the comprehensive creation and oversight of active, inactive, and prospective customer leads. Each customer is assigned a dedicated profile within the system, equipped with a personalized dashboard tailored to assess insightful metrics and analytics.
This dashboard provides valuable data on customer interactions, purchase history, and preferences, empowering sales personnel to make informed decisions and personalize their approach.
Moreover, the integration of sales cycle initiation directly from the customer dashboard streamlines the process, allowing for seamless transition from lead generation to conversion. Through this robust module, ArcFlow enables businesses to effectively manage their customer relationships and drive sales growth.
Process Flow:
￼

Sales Order Management
Overview Description:
Within the ArcFlow Sales Order Management Sub-Module, sales order management encompasses the comprehensive process of overseeing customer orders from inception to completion. This entails a series of steps, beginning with the creation of quotes and their subsequent conversion into sales orders.
The system facilitates the seamless generation of invoices and enables the tracking of purchased assemblies, products, and items as they progress through various stages of production. By providing real-time updates on pricing, order details, production status, and delivery schedules, the module ensures that all aspects of the sales order are efficiently managed and monitored. This comprehensive approach enhances transparency and communication between the sales team and customers, resulting in a seamless and satisfying experience for both parties.
Definitions:
Sales Quote
A sales quote is a document provided to a potential customer that outlines the estimated cost of a product or service. It includes details such as the quantity, unit price, and total price of the items being quoted. Sales quotes are typically used to initiate the sales process and provide customers with an understanding of the pricing for their desired products or services.
Note: During the sales cycle, you are able to skip the sales quote stage, but the initial step has to be the sales order. The sales order is feeder data into the manufacturing module which alerts the production team of up and coming orders for production.
Sales Order
A sales order is a formal request made by a customer to purchase goods or services. It includes specific details such as the quantity, description, and agreed-upon price of the items being ordered. Sales orders are generated based on the customer's acceptance of a sales quote and serve as a confirmation of the purchase.
Proforma Invoice
A proforma invoice is a preliminary bill of sale sent to buyers in advance of a shipment or delivery of goods. It details the types and quantities of products, their prices, and other important terms such as delivery and payment terms, but it is not a demand for payment. Proforma invoices are commonly used to provide an estimate or quote to the buyer, allowing them to review and approve the details before the final invoice is issued and the transaction is completed. This document helps ensure transparency and agreement on the terms of the sale before the actual transaction takes place.
Sales Invoice
A sales invoice is a document sent to the customer after the products or services have been delivered. It includes detailed information such as the itemized list of products or services provided, quantities, prices, any applicable taxes, and the total amount due. Sales invoices serve as a formal request for payment and provide a record of the transaction.

	•	Create Sales Order
1\. There are 2 ways to create a Sales Order. The first is to take a Sales Quote and convert it into a Sales Order. You do this by clicking this button on the Sales Quote page.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/1b80e48e-a44d-4f68-bb6d-c24ebed2782d/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1468,244&br_px=2328,725&force_format=png&width=860&wat_scale=76&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=432,212
2\. You can then review the details of the Sales Quote and make any necessary changes. If you are happy you can click Create.

Customer Returns
Overview Description:
It allows customers to request return authorisations and facilitates the receipt and inspection of returned items. The feature supports processing refunds or replacements and updating inventory records accordingly. It also provides detailed tracking and reporting on return reasons and statuses, ensuring that returns are handled swiftly and accurately to maintain customer satisfaction.
Customer Return Definitions:
During the customer return process you will be presented with the following key terms:
Warranty Status
During the warranty setup and creation process you created different warranty classes which we assigned to sellable items, assemblies and products. When you lodge a customer return, you enter in the serial number of the sold good and the system checks for any linked warranties.
You will be presented with the following warranty statuses upon serial number entry:
	•	No Warranty: There has been no warranties assigned to the sellable item, assembly or product. There will be no coverage for the customer.
	•	In Warranty: There has been an assigned warranty and the customer will receive a return or services in line with the created warranty coverage.
	•	Out of Warranty: There has been an assigned warranty, but the warranty expiration date has been reached and there is no longer an active warranty claim.
Issue Date
The Issue Date is the date in which the sellable item, assembly or product was sold or delivered to the customer. The issue date resembles the data in which the warranty is initiated for potential coverage.
Expiration Date
The Expiration Date is the date in which the warranty becomes inactive. This is calculated by adding the standard warranty duration for the assigned warranty to the date of issue outlined above. Any return before the expiration date will entitle warranty coverage.

Sales Configuration
Overview Description:
The Sales Configuration module in our system allows you to set up and manage pricing structures, including price breaks and percentage discounts. These discounts can be assigned to sellable products, assemblies, and individual items, or directly to specific customers. This flexibility enables you to create tailored pricing strategies that cater to various customer segments and sales scenarios, ensuring competitive and attractive pricing for your products while maximizing profitability and customer satisfaction.
Please find the descriptions below:
Price Breaks: A price break is a discount or reduction in the price of sellable stock based on the quantity purchased. Initially, price breaks are assigned to sellable stock items. They can also be assigned to specific customers, but only after being applied to the sellable stock. This mechanism reflects deviations in the price of an item depending on the quantity bought, thereby encouraging bulk purchases by offering lower prices for larger quantities.
Percentage Discounts: A percentage discount is a reduction in the price of an item based on a specified percentage, applied during the sale. This type of discount can be created specifically for a customer, which is a required field. Once established, the percentage discount can be assigned to sellable stock linked to that customer. A single percentage discount is added and applied at the time of sale, ensuring that the customer receives the agreed-upon discount on their purchases.

Warranties
Overview Description:
The ArcFlow warranty sub-module enables the creation of specific warranty classes that can be assigned to various sellable products, assemblies, and items.
This feature categorizes the coverage and details associated with a customer's returned product, assembly, or item. The coverage also specifies whether there is a fee or no fee charged to the customer for the returned order to be either replaced, repaired, and returned.
Key Definitions:
During the warranty creation process you will be presented with key terms. Please find the definitions of each term below:
Warranty Type
A warranty type is a classification within a system that defines the specific terms and conditions of a warranty provided for products, items, or assemblies. By categorizing warranties into different types, a business can more efficiently manage and apply the appropriate warranty terms to various products and ensure customers receive the correct support and service based on their purchase.
Start Date
The start date is the date in which the warranty becomes effective and the coverage is initiated. The system provides for warranties to become effective based on the data of sale or the date of delivery.
Duration
The duration is the amount of time in which the warranty is valid for and induces coverage of the sellable item, assembly or product.

Sales History
Overview Description:
Our Sales History module provides a comprehensive record of all past sales transactions. It allows you to view detailed information on each sale, including product details, quantities, prices, customer information, and dates of transactions. This module supports the analysis of sales trends, customer purchasing behavior, and product performance over time. By offering in-depth insights into historical sales data, the Sales History module helps you make informed business decisions, improve forecasting, and enhance customer relationship management.

Sales Dashboard
Overview Description:
The Sales Dashboard sub-module on the ArcFlow ERP system provides a real-time overview of sales performance through visual charting and metric collection. Users can filter date ranges to customize the displayed data. The dashboard tracks metrics such as sales volume, highest-performing sellable products, assemblies, and items, and shows customer segments based on sales volume. This comprehensive view helps businesses quickly assess their sales activities and make informed decisions.

Warehousing Overview
Warehousing Module Description
The Warehouse Module is responsible for inventory management, including tracking stock levels, managing warehouse operations, and organizing the storage and distribution of goods. It's key for maintaining efficient inventory control and order fulfilment.
The warehouse structure in the ERP system consists of four distinct levels: Site, Warehouse, Area, and Location. Users can create multiple instances of each level, which can be linked to their appropriate parent. After setting up the structure and allocating stock, users have the capability to transfer stock between different sites, warehouses, areas, and locations. Furthermore, they can receive stock items along with their quantities into the various levels of the warehouse structure.
The users can make use of the inventory management system to create stock take requisitions to conduct a physical stock count and compare the quantities for the respective stock items, assemblies and products to the virtual quantities on the ERP system.

Warehousing Sub Modules
	•	Warehousing
The warehousing sub module allows for the creation of the virtual representation of your physical warehousing structure. The sub module stored specific stock items, assemblies and products in certain and specified area types which act as feeder processes or data into manufacturing processes.

	•	Inventory Management
The inventory management sub module allows for the physical vs virtual stock count and the creation of stock take requisitions to update any stock discrepancies which storing a historical history of all previously created requisitions.

	•	Transfer History
The transfer history sub module displays a historical record of all transferred or received stock items, assemblies or products into the different sites, warehouses, areas or locations.

Warehousing
Overview Description:
The warehouse structure in the ERP system consists of four distinct levels: Site, Warehouse, Area, and Location. Users can create multiple instances of each level, which can be linked to their appropriate parent. After setting up the structure and allocating stock, users have the capability to transfer stock between different sites, warehouses, areas, and locations. Furthermore, they can receive stock items along with their quantities into the various levels of the warehouse structure.
￼

Definitions
Site
The site represents the physical address or location where your warehouse or warehouses are situated. It typically encompasses a broader geographical area and may include multiple buildings or facilities.
Warehouse
A warehouse refers to the actual physical building or structure where goods are stored. It is within the site and serves as the primary storage space for inventory items. Each warehouse can have its own unique characteristics and layout.
Area
An area within a warehouse serves as a designated section or zone dedicated to organizing and storing various types of inventories. These areas are categorized based on the specific type of items they hold, which may include finished goods, raw materials, sub-assemblies, scrap, and customer or supplier returns, among others.
The areas have the following pre-defined area types which are utilized to store specific types of stock inventory for different use cases:
	•	Raw Materials: Area for storing unprocessed materials that will be used in manufacturing.
	•	Finished Goods: Space designated for products that have completed the manufacturing process and are ready for sale.
	•	Quality Inspection: Zone where items are checked for quality assurance before they move to the next phase of production or shipping.
	•	Shipping and Receiving: Area dedicated to the arrival of incoming goods and the dispatch of outgoing orders.
	•	Sub-assembly Inventory: Section for storing partially assembled products that require further assembly before they become finished goods.
	•	Kitting Space: Where individual items are grouped, packaged, and supplied together as one unit, which is essential for assembly lines.
	•	Packaging: Area where products are packaged for storage or shipment, with materials like boxes, bubble wrap, and tape readily available.
	•	Scrap/Waste Disposal: Designated spot for the collection of unusable by-products or waste materials that are to be discarded or recycled.
	•	Tool Crib: Secure location where tools are stored and managed, often with check-in/check-out controls.
	•	Maintenance Area: Reserved for the upkeep and repair of machinery, equipment, and parts.
	•	Supplier Returns: Space allocated for storing items that are returned to suppliers due to defects, excess order, or other reasons.
	•	Customer Returns: Section for goods returned by customers that may be restocked, repaired, or processed in another manner.
	•	Special Storage: Area for items that require specific environmental conditions or security measures, such as high-value or hazardous materials.
	•	Temporary Storage: Flexible space used for short-term storage needs, often used for overflow or staging items for processing.
	•	Destroyed/Condemned: Area for goods that are marked to be destroyed due to irreparable damage or expiration.
	•	Repairs: Workspace for fixing damaged goods or equipment that can be returned to functional use.
Location
A location is the most detailed and specific storage designation within an area. It pinpoints the exact spot where an item is stored within the warehouse. Locations can be identified using various methods such as bin numbers, shelf numbers, or coordinates, and they help warehouse staff easily locate and retrieve items when needed.

Walkthrough Documentation:
	•	Creating a Site
Step 1
Select the “Create Site” button as seen below:
￼
Step 2
Enter in the following information to create the site:
	◦	Site Name
	◦	Site Street Address
	◦	Site State/Region
	◦	Site Country
	◦	Site Postal Code
	•	￼
Step 3
Once you have entered in the details of the site, you must select the “Create” button which will create the virtual representation of your physical site:
￼
Once you have created the site, it will be populated on left site and is ready to create the sub warehouses, areas and locations which form part of the newly created site:

Inventory Management
Overview Description:
The inventory management sub module is utilised to create stock take requisitions to conduct a physical stock count and compare the quantities for the respective stock items, assemblies and products to the virtual quantities on the ERP system.
Stock take requisitions can be created to record any stock discrepancies and update the virtual stock quantity balances to ensure the alignment of the physical stock quantities.
Inventory Management Process Flow:
￼
Overview Video:
Inv Man.mp4
Walkthrough Documentation:
	•	Inventory Management
Step 1
Select the “Inventory Management” button to view the current stock levels and create stock take requisitions.
￼
Step 2
The initial page will show you the current stock levels for all stock items for all warehouse sites and their associated warehouses, areas and locations.
You must select the appropriate Site, Warehouse and Area into which you would like to create a Stock Take Requisition for.
￼
Step 3
The specific destination will be populated with the assigned stock items. Select the “Generate Stock Take Requisition” button to action the stock take.
￼
Step 4
Specify if you would like to include serialization and batching for the Stock Take Requisition.
￼
Select the “Confirm” button
￼
Step 5
The Stock Take Requisition and been created and now you must select the “Stock Take Requisition” tab to view the pending requisitions.
￼
Step 6
Select the specific Stock Date Code you would like to complete:
￼
Step 7
Select the edit button next to each item code to enter in the correct stock values:
￼
￼
Step 8
Select the "Submit Requisition” button to submit the updated quantities.
￼
The stock take requisition will now be completed and then stock values will be updated in the specified location.

Transfer History
Overview Description:
The Transfer History sub-module meticulously records the entire history of stock transfers within the system. These stock transfers encompass movements between various sites, warehouses, areas, or specific locations within the organizational framework. Additionally, any stock received from suppliers and subsequently transferred from the receivable holding area to a designated warehouse is comprehensively documented within this module. This thorough record-keeping mechanism ensures transparency and accountability in the inventory management process, providing a detailed trail of stock movements for analytical purposes and operational insights.
Overview Video:
Transfer History.mp4
Walkthrough Documentation:
	•	Transfer History
Step 1
Select the “Transfer History” button to view a history of all the stock and associated data transferred or received into a specific warehouse destination:
￼
Step 2
A full history of all receipts and transfers will be populated with the stock items associated code, version, type, manufacturing batch number, manufacturing serial number, internal batch number, internal serial number, quantity, the warehouse it was transferred from and the destination warehouse along with the data in which the transfer or receipt occurred.
￼

\Procurement Overview
Procurement Module Description
This module is dedicated to the acquisition of goods and services, encompassing the management of supplier relationships, purchase orders, inventory levels, goods receiving, and invoice processing. It plays a vital role in ensuring that a business maintains the necessary materials and resources to sustain its operations.
The procurement module facilitates the creation and oversight of suppliers, subcontractors, and manufacturers involved in the procurement process of ordered items. Users can generate material orders to maintain accurate inventory levels for minimum stock requirements, demand forecasting, or to fulfill production plans.
Furthermore, the module enables the tracking and management of order plans through the creation and administration of RFQs (Request for Quotation) and Purchase Orders. Additionally, it provides functionality for managing received stock, including the creation of Goods Received Notes and the allocation of ordered items to specific warehouses.
Procurement Module Process Flow
￼
Procurement Sub Modules
	•	Create Material Order
The Create Material Order sub-module enables the development of order plans for purchasing items from suppliers. You can create material order plans based on various criteria, such as Order to Stock, ArcAI recommendations, Replenish Minimum Stock levels, or the requirements of a production order.

	•	Manage Order
The Manage Orders sub-module streamlines the administration of created order plans. It allows you to track progress, generate and manage RFQs and Purchase Orders, and oversee the receipt of ordered items, ensuring they are assigned to specific warehouses as needed.

	•	Vendors/Manufacturers
The Vendors/Manufacturers sub-module provides comprehensive tools for creating and managing your network of suppliers, subcontractors, and manufacturers. This module allows you to maintain detailed profiles for each vendor, including contact information, products or services offered, and historical performance data.

	•	Dashboard
The Procurement Dashboard in the ArcFlow ERP system is a comprehensive management tool that provides a detailed overview of your procurement activities. It tracks key metrics such as procurement volume, supplier performance, and open and pending order plans.


Create Material Order
Overview Description:
The Create Material Order Plan functionality enables the development of order plans for a list of items and their respective quantities. These order plans are essential for ensuring stock availability for inventory management or production purposes. Once created, order plans serve as the basis for generating RFQs (Requests for Quotations) and, subsequently, Purchase Orders.
Order Plan Creation Types:
The system supports four different type of materials order plan creation methodologies listed below:
Order to Stock
Order to Stock involves manually creating an order plan for maintaining stock levels. This process allows you to select items, assemblies, and products. If you choose an assembly or product, the system will automatically decompose the Bill of Materials (BOM) structure into its individual components.
ArcAI
ArcAI generates a list of items and their respective quantities to be included in an order plan. The system leverages multiple data inputs, such as demand, minimum stock holding, delivery duration, and over 40 additional data sets, to provide these suggestions.
Production Plan
During the production plan creation phase, the production manager can notify the procurement department to create a procurement order plan to meet the production plan's requirements for the necessary stock of assemblies and products. This allows for the direct creation of an order plan based on the specific needs of the production order.
Replenish Minimum Stock
The Replenish Minimum Stock functionality notifies you when an order plan needs to be created to maintain the minimum stock levels for items. The system suggests quantities to order based on the difference between the current stock levels and the established minimum stock quantity.

	•	Replenish Minimum Stock

Manage Orders
Overview Description:
The “Manage Orders” Sub Module serves as a comprehensive platform for creating and overseeing the entire life cycle of material order plans within the procurement process. Beginning with the initiation of quotes, this module empowers users to create purchase orders seamlessly, ensuring the procurement of necessary goods or services. As the ordered stock items are received, the module facilitates their efficient allocation, streamlining the process of replenishing inventory and optimizing warehouse management.
Definitions
Order Plan
An order plan is a comprehensive framework that consolidates ordered items, quantities, and linked suppliers, serving as the backbone of the procurement process. It facilitates the creation of quotes and purchase orders, streamlining procurement workflows and ensuring precise inventory management.
RFQ
A quote serves as a formal request sent to suppliers to assess pricing, availability, and delivery timelines for specific goods or services. It enables organizations to gather essential information from multiple suppliers before making a procurement decision. With the ability to create multiple quotes for the same ordered items from different suppliers, organizations can compare offers and negotiate terms to secure the most favorable deal. Additionally, the option to skip the quote stage and proceed directly to creating a purchase order based on existing order plans streamlines the procurement process, expediting the acquisition of needed items or services.
Purchase Order
A purchase order is a formal document issued by a buyer to a supplier, specifying the details of the goods or services to be purchased. It outlines the quantity, price, delivery terms, and other relevant information agreed upon between the buyer and the supplier. A purchase order serves as a legally binding contract between the buyer and the supplier, confirming the agreement reached during the procurement process.
Receivables and Goods Received Notes
A Goods Received Note (GRN) is a formal document acknowledging the receipt of items ordered as part of a purchase order. Multiple GRNs can be generated for a single purchase order. Upon creation of GRNs, the received stock is initially stored in the receivables area before being allocated to specific warehouses for storage, thereby updating inventory levels accordingly.

Step 1: Select the "Purchase Orders" Feature.

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-08/9ccd0825-5a0f-4b7b-9729-8690f7d3d954/user_cropped_screenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1810&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=456,393

Vendors/Manufacturers
Overview Description:
The “Vendor/Manufacturer” Sub Module is for the management and creation of suppliers, sub contractors and manufacturers. Each type has their own purpose on the ArcFlow system and feeds into different processes.
Definitions:
Suppliers
Suppliers are entities from whom you can purchase goods and services directly. They provide the materials, components, or products required for your production processes or business operations. The system allows you to manage and track your orders, deliveries, and payments with these suppliers, ensuring you have the necessary resources to meet your business needs.
Sub Contractors
Sub Contractors are specialized service providers that you can engage to perform specific tasks or processes as part of your overall production or project execution. Unlike suppliers who provide goods, sub contractors offer services such as assembly, installation, or maintenance. The ERP system helps you manage contracts, monitor the progress of subcontracted work, and ensure timely completion and quality standards.
Manufacturers
Manufacturers are entities that produce items that you may need for your operations. While you cannot place orders directly with manufacturers through the ERP system, you can link them to your items for tracking purposes. This linkage allows you to monitor the origin of your goods, ensuring traceability and quality control. By tracking manufacturers, you can also manage information about the production capabilities and certifications of the entities that produce your critical items.
Ordering Type Definitions:
The ArcFlow system allows for three separate ordering methodologies which are automated through the system. When you create a supplier or sub contractor, you need to select the ordering type. Please find the descriptions below:
Supplier System The Supplier System method involves sending the RFQ directly to the supplier's procurement or ERP system through established electronic data interchange (EDI) or other integration means. This process allows seamless communication and data exchange between your ERP system and the supplier's system. The supplier receives the RFQ in their system, processes it, and sends a response back to your ERP system. This method is efficient, reduces manual entry errors, and ensures faster processing.
In-House Capture In-House Capture involves preparing the RFQ within your ERP system and manually communicating it to the supplier. After generating the RFQ, it can be exported to a digital format or printed and then sent via email or mail to the supplier. The supplier sends their quotation back via email, mail, or fax, and it is manually entered into your ERP system. This method is simple and suitable for suppliers without sophisticated systems, but it requires more manual handling.
ArcFlow Hotlink System The ArcFlow Hotlink System utilizes a specialized platform to manage the sending and receiving of RFQs. After generating the RFQ within your ERP system, it is transmitted to the supplier through the ArcFlow platform. The supplier processes the RFQ and responds via the same platform, with the response then integrated back into your ERP system. This method centralizes communication and tracking, streamlining the procurement process and reducing manual errors.
Supplier and Subcontractor KPI Metrics:
Supplier Item KPI Metrics
Once you have created a supplier or subcontractor and have conduced multiple purchase orders for the items supplied by the supplier or subcontractor each item will have a KPI rating. The KPI rating is the performance rating for the specific item supplied by the supplier or subcontractor. The rating is based on multiple input metrics such as quality, costing, delivery times and stock availability etc. When creating a order plan, the system will present you with multiple suppliers or subcontractors tied to the specific ordered items and based on their KPI rating for the item, you are able to select the suitable supplier to send out an RFQ to.
Supplier KPI Metrics
The supplier KPI metrics tab will be presented once you have created a supplier or subcontractor and have run through multiple purchase orders. Our system will present an analytics tab found under “Supplier KPI Metrics” when viewing a supplier and subcontractor. The analytics will present metrics on Delivery Score, Quality Score, Quantity Score, Costing Score, Responsiveness Score and Present a supplier confidence interval to suggest the overall confidence for the supplier.

Dashboard
Overview Description:
The Procurement Dashboard on the ArcFlow system offers a comprehensive overview of your procurement activities through detailed metrics and visualizations. It tracks key metrics such as procurement volume categorized by paid, pending, and settled invoices. The dashboard includes dynamic charts and graphs that illustrate procurement volume trends over time, as well as detailed breakdowns of procurement by item and by supplier. This intuitive visualisation aids in monitoring spending patterns, identifying top suppliers, and managing invoice statuses, thereby enhancing your overall procurement efficiency and decision-making process.

Manufacturing Overview
Manufacturing Module Description
The manufacturing module enables the setup of your production facility by establishing production lines and workstations.
You can create production plans that are scheduled using work orders. Job cards can be generated and assigned to employees, who will receive tasks based on the linked processes of the assemblies' and products' routes.
This module streamlines manufacturing operations by allowing users to kit assemblies and final assemblies before production. Additionally, users can view and execute their daily tasks or processes derived from the scheduled production plans.
Manufacturing Sub Module Functionality Overview
￼
Manufacturing Module Process Flow
￼
Manufacturing Sub Modules
	•	Production Setup
The pre-production sub-module manages the initiation of production orders, which can originate from Sales Orders, Made to Stock requests, or ArcAI suggestions. It serves as the primary phase of the production workflow, where the generation of production orders initiates the subsequent processing stages within the production sub-module.

	•	Pre Production
The production sub-module streamlines the oversight of generated production orders. Initially, scheduling production orders is executed through works orders and job cards, supported by our capacity planning feature. Additionally, the production sub-module provides a live overview of scheduled production orders, along with their associated assemblies and products, as they progress through production lines and linked workstations.

	•	Production Operations
The post-production sub-module facilitates the handling of finished products requiring packing and dispatch, destined for either warehouse storage or customer delivery.

	•	Production Overview
The production history sub module gives a historical view and management of all completed production orders.

	•	Dashboard
The manufacturing dashboard gives real time insight and decision making capabilities on the current production process and future production considerations.

Production Setup
Overview Description:
A production facility is the virtual representation of the physical space where manufacturing processes take place. It typically includes a production floor, equipped with machinery, tools, and workstations organized into production lines.
At its core, a production facility serves as the operational hub where raw materials are transformed into finished products or assemblies. It hosts various manufacturing processes, such as assembly, fabrication, machining, and quality control checks.
Production facilities comprise various production lines, each tailored to specific manufacturing processes. Within these production lines, there are multiple workstations, each designated for distinct tasks and operations. This hierarchical structure ensures that different stages of production are efficiently organized and managed.
Each workstation plays a critical role in the overall production line, contributing to the seamless flow of materials and assembly of products. By segmenting the production facility into specialized lines and workstations, the facility can optimize workflow, enhance productivity, and maintain high standards of quality control throughout the manufacturing process.
Production Setup Representation
Once you have setup your production facility, production line and workstations, the setup will create a virtual production facility environment. A visual example is found below:
￼
Key Terms:
Workstation production capacity refers to the maximum number of concurrent processes that can be performed. For instance, if a workstation has a production capacity of 2, this could mean either one employee can handle two processes simultaneously, or it could mean two employees can work on a single process concurrently.
The production capacity directly relates to the number of employees working concurrently at a workstation or the number of processes that can be executed simultaneously.

Pre Production
Overview Description:
The Pre-Production module encompasses all workflows and activities that take place before the commencement of actual production. This module is designed to help you efficiently create detailed production plans and schedules, which are managed through the generation of work orders and job cards. By providing a structured approach to planning, the module ensures that all necessary preparations are in place before production begins.
In addition to planning and scheduling, the Pre-Production module offers robust tracking capabilities, allowing you to monitor the progress of your production plans in real-time. This feature enables you to oversee the status of each planned task, identify any potential delays or issues, and make necessary adjustments to keep the production process on track. Through its comprehensive planning and tracking functionalities, the Pre-Production module ensures that your production operations are well-coordinated and poised for success.
Definitions:
Create Production Plan Type
When creating a production plan you can utilise the four method listed below:
	•	Sales Order: You create a production plan based on sales orders generated by the sales department to fulfil a customer order.
	•	Make to Stock: You create a production plan for the purposes of increasing your stock holding for assemblies and products.
	•	ArcAI: The ArcFlow system suggests which assemblies and products and their associated quantities you should produce based on production forecasting.
	•	Able to Manufacture: The system alerts you on which assemblies and products you are able to manufacture based on your stock availability.
Production Plan
A production plan is developed from sales orders and made-to-stock requirements. It outlines the overall strategy and schedule for manufacturing products, specifying what needs to be produced, in what quantities, and by when, to meet customer demands and maintain optimal inventory levels.
Work Order
A work order is generated to execute the production plan. You can have multiple work orders linked to a production plan. It contains the schedule and the different assemblies and products and their associated quantities which need to be executed. Work orders guide the production process, ensuring that each step is carried out according to the plan.
Job Card
Job cards are created to schedule and manage work orders. You can create multiple job cards to fulfil a work order. They are assigned to employees and detail the specific tasks they need to perform as part of the assembly or product route. Job cards help in organizing the workflow, tracking progress, and ensuring that each task is completed efficiently and accurately.

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/fd300d97-6c52-4c96-9a47-6420359908e9/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,63&br_px=3439,1986&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=74,286

Production Operations
Overview Description:
The Production Operations Sub Module is an operational tool utilised by the factory floor workers during the production process.
It facilitates the kitting of assemblies and final assemblies prior to embarking on their manufactured routes for either as an assembly or product.
Users are able to view their jobs allocated to them, the instructions for the process linked to the job and also the workstations in which are assigned to to complete the job.
Definitions
Sub Assembly Kitting Area
The Sub Assembly Kitting Area marks the beginning of an assembly's journey along its route. Here, users can access a comprehensive list of all the items required for assembly, enabling them to gather and group these components efficiently to progress through the sub assembly route.
Final Assembly Kitting Area
The Final Assembly Kitting Area marks the beginning of the final assemblies journey along its route. Here, users can access a comprehensive list of all the items and assemblies required for the final assembly, enabling them to gather and group these components efficiently to progress through the final assembly route.
Note: before any assemblies and products can be initiated through their route using job cards, you will need to action the sub assembly and final assembly kitting areas before the components are pushed through to production. Essentially, step 1 of every production process is to kit the sub assembly or final assembly so all the necessary components are gathered prior to the production processes and routing.
Jobs
Jobs are created and assigned to employees which form part of a Work Order. These jobs are directly associated with particular processes that must be executed as part of the manufacturing route for an assembly or product.
Workstations
A workstation is a designated area within a production line where employees gather to perform their assigned tasks and related processes.
Processes
A Process is associated with a job card, detailing tasks for an employee to carry out. These processes occur at workstations and involve three main stages: Input, Process, and Output. The Input comprises the collection of items or assemblies, while the Process entails utilizing instructions and tools to transform the Input into an Output. This Output represents the completed task, which subsequently serves as the Input for the next process along the manufacturing route for the assembly or product.
Process Flow

	•	Allocated Jobs and Performing Processes
Step 1: Select "Jobs"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/8455a7dd-fd3a-4ebb-8932-fdd2944d0bbf/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=419,186
Step 2: The user will view all the jobs allocated to them. The user will select the specific job to complete the process.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/3e067043-4744-4895-822b-cc7278ddeca9/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=142,191
Step 3: The user will view the inputs received for this task, the process which needs to be completed and submit the output. The user will start by selecting "Receive and Start". Will means that the user confirm that they have received the input stock and have initiated the process.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/45a2c440-d546-4d07-838a-9578e68aef7b/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=16,0&br_px=3456,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=985,214
Click "Start"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/250a7403-c6dd-43fc-9028-102f47400b10/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1098,673&br_px=2818,1634&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=524,277
Step 4: Select "Process"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/b2227dd9-537a-4773-bdac-c92fa3ba5062/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=2293,1281&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=440,256
The process will outline the tools and instructions needed to transform the input into the desired output during this process in the associated manufactured route. Upon completion, the user must select the "Output" tab.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/e6d2fd1b-422a-4ac6-89e6-34ca7ed0bdae/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=0,0&br_px=3439,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=426,148
Step 5: The output tab will display the expected output and the associated quantity. Upon process completion, the user must enter in the quantity in which they will submit which will feed into the next process in the route.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/e84a8a27-5594-433a-bb9c-8c20ce8eaf4f/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=16,0&br_px=3456,1922&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=892,217
Step 6: The user must select "Submit"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/2e2f26c6-4069-4c2d-8d4a-2992da4edf08/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1162,135&br_px=3456,1416&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=936,277
Step 7: The user will select their name in the dropdown which gives an audit trail of who completed the process.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/ae15d68a-b547-425f-abe3-3f9470dbed5c/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=944,587&br_px=2664,1548&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=524,277
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/dc95a69f-5204-494d-83b1-27a700c823c3/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=872,823&br_px=2592,1784&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=524,276
Step 8: Select "Submit" which will state that the process has been completed and the output will feed as an input into the next process.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/f8bc8a8c-888b-476a-a8b8-d307a5de7c0e/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=970,709&br_px=2690,1670&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=524,277

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/e09793da-862a-4863-a549-74b6e02faeab/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1736,241&br_px=3456,1202&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=619,277

!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/818e2973-afb9-4f2f-bec4-edbd79272077/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1736,21&br_px=3456,982&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=905,277
Click "Confirm"
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-06-02/02dac9a7-3ffb-420b-af0c-1c15e65835d1/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1110,677&br_px=2830,1638&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=524,276

Production Overview
Overview Description:
The Production Overview Sub-Module serves as a comprehensive management tool, enabling you to monitor the real-time status of work-in-progress across various aspects of your production operations. This includes tracking the activities of employees, the performance and utilization of workstations, and the current state of assemblies and products in the manufacturing process.
One of the key features of this sub-module is its ability to provide a detailed, real-time snapshot of ongoing production activities. Managers can observe the progress of tasks assigned to employees, assess the efficiency and capacity of workstations, and follow the assembly and production stages of products. This real-time insight helps in making informed decisions, identifying bottlenecks, and ensuring that production schedules are adhered to.
Additionally, the Production Overview Sub-Module offers a comprehensive historical view of all manufactured assemblies and products. This historical data allows for thorough analysis and review of past production runs, facilitating continuous improvement and optimization of manufacturing processes.

Dashboard
Overview Description:
The ArcFlow manufacturing dashboard provides both real-time and historical views of key manufacturing performance metrics. The dashboard features comprehensive metrics and charting capabilities, allowing you to track production volumes, failure rates, risk profiles, and outputs from employees and workstations. Additionally, it offers capacity analysis to ensure optimal utilization of resources and to identify potential bottlenecks in the production process.
Walkthrough Documentation:
	•	Manufacturing Dashboard
Fulfilment Overview
Fulfilment Module Description
The Fulfilment module oversees the processing of customers' completed sales orders, encompassing picking, packing, and customer delivery. Here are the five steps involved in this process:
	•	Completed Sales Orders: Real-time visibility into the progress of picking, packing, and customer delivery is provided through completed sales orders.
	•	Picking Slip Generation: Picking slips are generated, detailing the sellable products, assemblies, and quantities for warehouse staff to pick from inventory.
	•	Boxing and Labels: Selected products, assemblies, and items are packed into boxes and labeled for identification and shipping purposes.
	•	Holding Area: Packed boxes are temporarily housed in a designated area for final checks and verification before shipment.
	•	Shipping: Verified orders are dispatched for customer delivery, facilitated by shipping labels and accompanying documentation.
Fulfilment Module Process Flow
￼
Fulfilment Sub Modules
	•	Fulfilment
The Fulfilment module oversees the processing of customers' completed sales orders, encompassing picking, packing, and customer delivery.

	•	Fulfilment History
The fulfilment history provides a record of all completed orders, detailing their processing journey from order receipt to delivery. It offers insights into order status, tracking information, and any actions taken during the fulfilment process, serving as a valuable reference for tracking order progress and resolving any issues that may arise.

Fulfilment
Overview Description:
The Fulfilment module oversees the processing of customers' pending and completed sales orders, encompassing picking, packing, and customer delivery.
Processes and Definitions:
Pending and Completed Sales Orders
Real-time visibility into the progress of picking, packing, and customer delivery is provided through completed sales orders.
Picking Slip Generation
Picking slips are generated, detailing the sellable products, assemblies, and quantities for warehouse staff to pick from inventory.
Boxing and Labels
Selected products, assemblies, and items are packed into boxes and labeled for identification and shipping purposes.
Holding Area
Packed boxes are temporarily housed in a designated area for final checks and verification before shipment.
Shipping
Verified orders are dispatched for customer delivery, facilitated by shipping labels and accompanying documentation.
Establishing Packaging Materials:
During the fulfilment process you need to box the completed goods to be delivered to your customers. This will entail having packaging materials available for packaging purposes. You will create these items through the blueprints module by either creating an assembly or items and tag them with the following attributes:
Is Shipping Container
If you tag an item as “Is Shipping Container” the system will store this items as a container for packaging completed sellable stock for customer delivery. These items will be presented in the fulfilment module when you need to allocate packaging materials for customer deliveries. An example of this type of item will be a wooden pallet.
Is Shipping Supplies
If you tag an Item as “Is Shipping Supplies” the system will store the item for the purposes of protecting sellable stock inside the shipping container. An example of this type of item would be bubble wrap.
Once you have created these assemblies or items and added stock quantity to your appropriate warehouses, they will then be populated during the “Box and Label” process in fulfilment. You are not able to box and label if you do not have sufficient stock on hand.

Fulfilment History
Overview Description:
The Fulfilment History sub-module provides a comprehensive historical overview of all your fulfilled orders.
Within this sub-module, you can meticulously track orders and their associated details, offering valuable insights into your fulfilment process. You will be able to view critical information such as the Sales Order Number, Date of Shipment, and Date of Arrival. Additionally, it includes details about the different shipping partners involved and the corresponding waybill numbers linked to each delivery. This level of detail allows you to monitor and analyse your fulfilment operations effectively, ensuring you have a clear understanding of your order delivery history and performance.
Overview Video:
FulHistory.mp4
Walkthrough Documentation:
	•	Fulfilment History
Step 1
Select the “Transfer History” button to view a history of all the stock and associated data transferred or received into a specific warehouse destination:
￼
Step 2
A full history of all receipts and transfers will be populated with the stock items associated code, version, type, manufacturing batch number, manufacturing serial number, internal batch number, internal serial number, quantity, the warehouse it was transferred from and the destination warehouse along with the data in which the transfer or receipt occurred.
￼

Document Hub Overview
Document Hub Module Description
The ArcFlow "Document Hub" serves as a centralized document repository for viewing and managing all documents uploaded onto the system, pertaining to various actions such as:
	•	Items
	•	Assemblies
	•	Products
	•	Node Items
	•	Suppliers
	•	Customers
	•	Manufacturers
	•	Subcontracted Routes
	•	Sales Persons
	•	GRN Delivery Notes
	•	Warranties
Document Module Process Flow
￼
Document Hub
Overview Description:
The ArcFlow "Document Hub" serves as a centralized document repository for viewing and managing all documents uploaded onto the system, pertaining to various actions such as:
	•	Items
	•	Assemblies

	•	Document Hub
Step 1: Click the "Document Hub" Module.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-06/d6a495b6-4979-4e55-83a1-ba6b2c8c378b/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=16,63&br_px=3456,1986&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=660,489

	•	AI Functionality Overview
	•	AI Functionality Description
	•	ArcFlow leverages AI technology to enhance manufacturers' productivity with existing resources. By automating repetitive tasks, the system optimizes resource allocation and enhances decision-making efficiency.
	•	The AI models leverage over 100 input data points, which are stored, analyzed, and processed to generate outputs that support accurate decision-making. These models improve over time as more transactions occur and historical data accumulates, allowing for continuous training and enhancement of the models' accuracy.
	•	At its core, ArcFlow offers three AI-driven features: Supplier KPI and Selection, Order Plan Automation, and Production Order Automation.
	•	AI Model Diagram
	•	The AI model comprises of:
	•	Input Parameters: the raw data sets which are fed into the Input Layers.
	•	Input Layer: Extracts the meaningful and relevant data from the Input Parameters.
	•	Hidden Layers: Analyses the data and their respective importance weighting and adjustments overtime into the AI model to create accurate AI model outputs.
	•	AI Output: The results of the computations to create an accurate suggestive output.
	•	￼
	•	AI Functionality Features:
	•	Supplier KPI and Selection
Streamline and automate supplier selection decisions during the procurement process.

	•	Order Plan Automation
Automating the order plan creation for optimal quantities and timing for ordering specific materials.

	•	Production Order Automation
Automating production order creation and scheduling for different products and assemblies with their associated quantities.

Supplier KPI and Selection
Overview Description:
The Suppliers KPI and Selection model evaluates supplier performance based on various metrics such as the quality of items supplied, overall performance, delivery efficiency, and cost. These KPI metrics are integrated into a supplier selection model, which helps the system recommend the best suppliers to order from during the quoting and purchase order stages, considering specific constraints.

Module Dependancy Overview
ArcFlow Interconnected and Module Dependancy Overview
The interconnected nature of the ArcFlow system ensures a smooth flow of data across its various modules. This connectivity paves the way for heightened automation and more efficient workflows within the system.
In this current overview, we'll delve into the dependencies between different modules and provide insights into how users should navigate and anticipate the completion of workflow processes.
Module Dependancy Focus Points:
	•	Production and Routing
The production of assemblies and products depends on creating eligible routes for each assembly and product. After creating your items, assemblies, and products in the blueprints module, you must establish their manufacturing routes.

	•	Warehouse Stock, Kitting and Job Cards
When initiating a production process by creating a production plan, there are two key dependencies that must be addressed before a job card can be initiated by a system user who has access to the “Manufacturing Operations” Sub Module.

	•	Warehousing and Fulfilment
The fulfillment module handles the picking, packing, and dispatch of customer deliveries. To ensure smooth operations, all stock intended for delivery must be stored in a Finished Goods area.

Routing and Production
Overview Description:
The production of assemblies and products depends on creating eligible routes for each assembly and product. After creating your items, assemblies, and products in the blueprints module, you must establish their manufacturing routes.
A product comprises multiple child assemblies and items, with each child assembly having its own BOM (Bill of Materials) structure, including further child assemblies and items. Each level of an assembly's BOM structure requires a manufacturing route, which then integrates into the higher-level route of the products it is linked to.
The routing of a product begins with manufacturing all sub-assemblies according to their respective manufacturing routes. Once these assemblies are manufactured, they become inputs for the product's manufacturing route, continuing until the finished product is complete.
It is crucial to note that you cannot manufacture an assembly or product without an established manufacturing route.
Overview Video:
Routing and Production.mp4
Warehouse Stock, Kitting and Job Cards
Overview Description:
When initiating a production process by creating a production plan, there are two key dependencies that must be addressed before a job card can be initiated by a system user who has access to the “Manufacturing Operations” Sub Module.
Job cards are dependent on the kitting processes for sub-assemblies or final assemblies. A user cannot start a job card if the items or assemblies required for the job are not kitted and pushed to production.
In the kitting module, users will see a list of items and assemblies to be kitted for a specific manufacturing route and its associated job cards. Kitting can only proceed if there is sufficient stock available in the warehouse for the required items or assemblies.
Essentially, warehouse stock is needed for kitting, and job cards can only be initiated once the necessary materials have been kitted. During the assembly route, the process concludes with storing the assembly in the appropriate Sub Assembly Warehouse. This sub-assembly stock, once the route is completed, will then be used in the final assembly kitting area for the product's final production processes which is then stored in the Finished Goods Warehouse.
Inter Connectivity Diagram:
￼
Warehousing and Fulfilment
Overview Description:
The fulfillment module handles the picking, packing, and dispatch of customer deliveries. To ensure smooth operations, all stock intended for delivery must be stored in a Finished Goods area.
During the picking process, the fulfillment module only checks stock availability in the Finished Goods warehouse. At the end of the production process, finished goods are stored in this warehouse, marking the completion of the process.
However, there are unique situations to consider. If you have an item or assembly that is sellable but currently stored in an Item Warehouse or Sub-Assembly Warehouse, you must transfer this stock to the Finished Goods area to fulfill customer orders.
Even if an item or assembly is sellable, if it is not stored in the Finished Goods area, the system will not recognize its availability during the fulfillment stage, and you will be unable to process the delivery. Therefore, ensure all sellable stock is transferred to the Finished Goods area before fulfillment.
Inter Connectivity Diagram:
￼
Overview Video:
Warehouse and Fulfilment.mp4
Overview and Documentation Templates
ArcFlow Automated Document Generation Overview
During manufacturing operations and processes, ArcFlow captures essential information from customers, suppliers, employees, stock, and sellable items, as well as assemblies and products. This system meticulously records and organizes data, ensuring all critical aspects of production are monitored and documented. By automating the generation of necessary documentation, ArcFlow streamlines workflow and reduces the administrative burden on your team. This automation ensures accuracy and efficiency, allowing you to focus more on core business activities while maintaining comprehensive records.
The following documents are generated below:
Procurement
	•	Request for Quotation with Online Review Button
	•	Request for Quotation without Online Review Button
	•	Purchase Orders
	•	Goods Received Note
Blueprints
	•	Assemblies
	•	Products
Manufacturing
	•	Picking Slip
	•	Packing Slip
Sales
	•	Sales Quotation with Discount
	•	Sales Quotation without Discount
	•	Sales Order with Discount
	•	Sales Order without Discount
	•	Proforma Invoice with Discount
	•	Proforma Invoice without Discount
	•	Sales Invoice with Discount
	•	Sales Invoice without Discount
	•	Picking Slip
	•	Packing Slip
	•	Customer Return
Storage of Documents
The storage of all of the auto generated documents are found under the “Document Hub” module. Generated documents will be categorised and stored in the document repository for tracking and viewing purposes.
ArcFlow Automated Document Templates
	•	Procurement

In-App Support Functionality
Overview Description:
ArcFlow engineers will provide real-time support through messaging, screen sharing, and audio features, ensuring your operations continue smoothly without disruptions.
Walkthrough Documentation:
	•	In-App Support
Step 1: Select the chat icon at the top right of your screen.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/a2ee9fd3-176e-4664-9c78-673ad91afd06/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1736,0&br_px=3456,961&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=915,13
Step 2: Enter in your name
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/42bd13fb-8f0e-4665-a173-a6c57d3100e7/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=16,63&br_px=3456,1986&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=910,418
Step 3: Enter in your Email Address
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/88b0f520-b6f5-485e-9ffc-ec33fe5e864b/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1736,1024&br_px=3456,1986&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=724,332
Step 4: Select the "Start the Chat" button. You will be connected with an ArcFlow engineer and will be able to utilise real time messaging, audio communication and screen sharing.
!https://ajeuwbhvhr.cloudimg.io/colony-recorder.s3.amazonaws.com/files/2024-05-30/2aa60194-7615-44f7-a98e-bba9d2fb8c9b/ascreenshot.jpeg?tl_px=1736,1024&br_px=3456,1986&force_format=png&width=1120.0&wat=1&wat_opacity=0.7&wat_gravity=northwest&wat_url=https://colony-recorder.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/images/watermarks/FB923C_standard.png&wat_pad=789,403
